BASIC CELERITY

ALACRICY



Your reflexes are so well developed that you can respond to another's actions

-evenas he begins to move. With the expenditure of a Blood Trait, you can preempe:

any physical actions you are aware of that take place in a turn. Should a yeoman.

abruptly switch from parlaying with you to attempting to impale you with his spear :

you may choose to attack him first. Should the same yeoman attempt to shoot you

with his longbow with no warning, this ability will aid you not at all.



SWIRTNESS



. You can move with speed greater than that of any mortal. With the expen:

diture of a Blood Trait, in addition to the benefits of Alacrity, you are allowed.an

additional physical action that takes place after all other actions are completed



INTERMEDIATE CELERITY

RAPIDITY



Your speed bewilders even other supernaturally fast creatures. With the

expenditure of a Blood Trait, in addition to the benefits of Swiftness, you may use

the Bomb in challenges that depend on speed or agility, but not on strength. You

must warn your opponent that you can use the Bomb, and how it works before the



challenge. You may — but are not required to — use the Bomb in any challenges

throughout the turn.



LEGERITY



You move faster than the eyes of mortals can follow. With the expenditure of

a Blood Trait, in addition to the benefits of Rapidity, you can take a third action, |

which takes place after all actions of vampires using Swiftess.



ADVANCED CELERITY

FLEETNESS



You are like the wind — and often, the wind your passing stirs is all that 18

detected of you. With the expenditure of a Blood Trait, in addition to the benefits



gerity, You automatically win all ties involving your speed or agility, regardless



ourtelative Traits. Should you use this against a Cainite using a Discipline with

similar effect (such as Potence’s Puissance), neither vampire has the advantage

f ties are resolved as normal.



ELDER CELERITY

QUICKNESS



- -Proubadours have claimed that you outpace lightning. With the expenditure

fa Blood Trait, in addition to the benefits of Fleetness, you can take a fourth

ction, which takes place after the actions of all vampires using Legevity.



HIMERSTRY



Only the Ravnos claim a native talent with Chimerstry, the Discipline of

lusions, and its fabled origins are as sacrilegious as its users. Some claim that the

lan founder stole the Devil’s flair for deceit, while others whisper that he gained

t by drinking the blood of a faerie. Since these fables originate with the Raynos,

ew lend them any credence. Devout philosophers claim that C ‘himerstry leads

ainites further astray by entrapping them in their own illusions.



Chimerstry can add to something's appearance but not subtract from it, Itcan lay

‘an illusion over certain features but not make it unnoticeable — such is the

rovenance of Obfuscate. Additionally, even tactile illusions cannot support wei ght

ot provide more than the sensation of resistance, so illusory bars over a dungeon

window could feel solidly real, but one who threw herselfat them would pass through.

--Hhusions created with Chimerstry are real to the fae, and even a longsword

reated with Ignis Fatwus that would not be felt by an ordinary mortal can cause

njure faerie creatures.



Players might wish to work with Storytellers in advance to prepare item cards

_for the subjects of their illusions. Use Subterfuge for retests of Chimerstry.



BASIC CHIMERSTRY

_ IGNIS RATUUS



You can create a brief, unmoving image that affects a single sense. You could

_ Make'a person smell roses, feel the touch of a breeze, hear the sound of rats scurrying

oF sée’'a coffer of jewels. These illusions lack substance, and cannot in and of

themselves harm someone. If it is visible, you, and you alone, can pick up and move

_ the illusion. Others merely pass through it, and it has no movement of its own.

Expend a Willpower Trait and engage your targets in a Social Challenge. If you

Win, your illusion exists as you describe it until you dismiss it (which is instanta-

Neous and requires no action on your part), you leave the area or the illusion is

disproved (by having a hand pass through it, for example).



You can craft illusions that affect all the senses you desire, however, they are

still lusions, An illusory dagger may look sharp and feel sharp if someone tests its

edge’ but its slash will not even crease flesh. These illusions do not move under

their own power, but others can handle them. The illusory dagger could be tos



toa friend, and it would move as any real dagger. Expend a Willpower Trait and 2

a Blood Trait, and engage your targets ina Social Challenge. Ifyouwin, the illusion

exists under the same conditions as a creation of Ignis Fatuus. :

APPARITION



You can give motion to illusions created with Ignis Fats or Dweomer: The

motion may be simple asa tree bending in the wind or complex asa knight in armor

charging with his broadsword ready. It is a boon if you are familiar with that which

your illusion imitates, for witnesses who find the motion to be unrealistic are mare

likely to pierce the illusion.

INTERMEDIATE DAIMOINON

ESSENCE OF THE NETHERWORLD



You can reach beyond what is and grasp the energies of the outer darkness ti

unleash upon Creation. These energies erode wood and stone, twist metal beyon

recognition and melt flesh, living or undead. Although these energies usuall

manifest as an ebon flame, certain Baali hurl strange lightning, pulses of shimmer

ing force, swarms of alien insects or other terrible forms of destruction. TK

servants of each master usually manifest only one form of power.



Begin crafting a mystic projectile in your hands, Each turn, you can expend 6

Blood Trait add power to the missile so that it inflicts one level ofageravated dama:

Since this power comes from beyond, you can only increase it at a rate of one Bloo

Trait/ one level of aggravated damage per turn regardless of your generation.



Releasing the missile is a standard ranged attack that can be dodged as usual. Arma

and inanimate objects without any mystical power are easily destroyed by Essence

the Netherworld, and they provide only half their usual protection.

crystallizing your victim’s sins into an allegorical opponent that only he cat

perceive, and thus drawing him into a morality play all bis own.

INTERMEDIATE FORTITUDE

RESILIENCE



Fire and sunlight still burn you, but not with the hideous intensity with whi

they affect other Cainites. When you suffer aggravated damage, perform a Sin

Test. If you win, one level of the damage taken is considered lethal rather th

aggravated. If you wish, you may spend a Stamina-related Physical Trait before y

make the test so that you win a tie.



Using Resilience is reflexive and does not count as an action. You mayonk

Resilience once for a given source of damage. If you suffer three levels of dama

froma rake of the claws of a werewolf, only one level converts to lethal; the otk

two levels remain aggravated.



RESISTANCE



You can shrug off blows that would leave a mortal staggering. When yousu

lethal or bashing damage, make a Simple Test. If you win, you may remove 6

level of damage from that suffered. If you wish, you may spend a Stamina-relat

Physical Trait before you make the test so that you win on a tie.



Using Resistance is reflexive and does not count as an action, You. may. us

Resistance on damage that was reduced to lethal from aggravated by Resilience. ¥

may only use Resistance once for a given source of damage.

_ BASIC CORPSE IN THE MONSTER



Masque of Death ;



You can grant yourself or another the appearance of an aged corpse. Expend

Blood Trait. If you wish to place this effect upon another, you must touch him

which may call fora Physical Challenge). If the recipient is willing, that suffices.

f not, you must defeat her ina Mental Challenge. Once the effect begins, flesh

draws taut, and the body takes on an entirely corpselike appearance and texture.

Those wearing the Masque of Death are one Trait down on all Social

Challenges except for intimidation purposes — for intimidation challenges, they

are one Trait up. Additionally, the Masque of Death stiffens its targets, rendering

thein-one Trait down on Physical Challenges involving flexibility and speed.



-- Vfone wearing the Masque of Death attempts to emulate a corpse, it takes a

successful Social Challenge to see through the disguise.



The Masque of Death ordinarily lasts until che next sunset, but the caster may



This power cannot be used to wither vital organs, as these are too far insid

the body.



Corrupt the Undead Flesh



You are capable of infecting a victim with a contagious mystical disease tha

merges the states of life, death and undeath. Those who suffer from the diséasi

experience a wide range of symptoms, including lethargy, weakness, dizziness, 1035

of blood control and loss of coordination. Although mortals can contract this

disease merely by being in the presence of a one already affected, Cainites inust-

drink the blood of a victim to be infected.



You must be able to see your victim. Spend a Willpower Trait and perform a.

challenge of your Mental Traits against your Target’s Physical Traits. [f you win,

your target is infected.



Infected Cainites lose one-quarter of their Mental and Physical Traits (round up) and

must spend two Blood Traits instead of one at the beginning of each night. Additionally,

Cainites must win a Static Self-Control} Instinct Challenge (difficulty of three Traits) each

time they feed or vomit back all the blood they just ingested without gaining any benefit

from it. Infected mortals lose one-quarter of their Mental and Physical Traits (round up);

take a level of lethal damage each night and cannot hold down any food. terminate it earlier.



Cold of the Grave ;

The dead feel no pain, and with this power, you can extend the same numbing

chill to yourself, The Cold of the Grave turns one’s skin cold to the touch and makes

all matters seem unimportant, even personal injury.



Expend one Willpower Trait. Your body and mind become unnaturally cold.

Yow are unaffected by wound penalties. You also gain a free retest against all

attempts to manipulate your emotions —- on the other hand, others receive a free

fetest on your attempts to manipulate their emotions. This chill does not reach the

Beast, however — you still frenzy under the same provocation.



At sunset cach evening, the victim may attempt to throw off the disease by

engaging in a Static Physical Challenge (difficulty seven Traits). With: the

acquisition of three successes, the disease has been conquered, and the chatactet

regains Traits at the rate of one per hour. Wounds recover at their usual rate.

OBFUSCATE



The Children of Caine are a blight on God’s creation; this Discipline allow

them to conceal their accursed selves from Gods children. Obfuscate does not off

true invisibility, rather it encourages those around the vampire to see him 4

something else or ignore him altogether, thus its effects extend even to the blin

or those relying on other senses. Some claim that Obfuscate points to the accurse

nature of Cainites, for it fosters isolation fromh umanity. Orhers suggest that Cain

taught it to the Nosferatu Antediluvian in hopes that he would conceal the visag

of himself and his childer. The infidel Assamites contest both notions, claiming

that Obfuscate represents a natural honing of their hunting prowess.



See Auspex (p. 157) for details on how that Discipline can penetrat

Obfuscate’s concealment.



Use Stealth for retests of Obfuscate.



In order to indicate your concealed status, cross your arms in front of

your chest, displaying a number of fingers on each hand corresponding to

your highest level of Obfuscate (one for Basic, two for Intermediate, three for



Advanced and four for Elder),

of Hell. This darkness is most commonly referred to as Ahriman — the dark half

of Zoroastrian dualism. Whatever it is, che darkness seems to have a will of its ow)

and it haunts and devours those who fail to master it.

BASIC POTENCE

PROWESS



Your strength is great even fora Cainite, and your blows stagger any opponen

You can choose to inflict lethal damage rather than bashing on any unarined

attacks or attacks using blunt weapons. Additionally, once per night, you'can

and Wiry Traits. These Traits must all be restored at the same time. If yow have 72

unexpended Traits at the time you decide to recover your strength, you cannot

restore them later in this fashion. Using Prowess does not require an action, and it

may be done any time, even when unconscious. ,



MIGHT



Your strength is obviously greater than any mere mortal’s, and even’ other

vampires consider it daunting. You may make a single retest on any challeng



involving sheer physical strength, such as breaking statuary, grappling with ==



peasants and lifting portcullises. Once you use Might for a retest, other retests'are



finesse or stamina rather than strength. (Your strength allows even glancing blows:

to do damage.) Might does not help in situations where agility is more useful; such

as throwing boulders.



INCERMEDIATE POTENCE

VIGOR



Your unnatural strength allows you to easily lift hundreds of pounds and crush:

bones with but a single blow. You may use the Bomb in challenges of strength. You

do not have to use it, but you must warn your opponent that you can use it and how

it works. Your opponent may use agility or finesse against your strength, but as long

as your strategy depends upon personal might, you may use the Bomb.



INTENSITY



Your might is unflagging, and under all but the most strenuous circumstances,

you can use your phenomenal strength without rest. You can use Potence as your

bid Trait in any challenges of strength. Even if you lose the challenge, you do niet

lose this Trait, so you may use it repeatedly. This Potence Trait does not countin

any other way, though. It cannot help in ties or overbid situations. You may not.

bid Potence twice in the event that you must bid more than one Trait. In those cases

your other bid Traits are at risk. Should you lose all of your Physical Traits, you

— FORGE



Your strength is the stuff of legends; you are a walking siege engine. In any

PRESENCE



Presence is the discipline of unnatural charisma. Tes practitioners command

he attention of those around them, draw prey to their sides with no more than a

eckoning glance, and draw out all variety of passions from their subjects. Whereas

Dominate bends the will of its victims to that of the Cainite, Presence sways their

emotions. This can be a great boon if the vampire prefers having lackeys with

nitiative and wits, but itcan also result in unpleasant surprises as each follower has

his'own vision of what the Cainite really wants. Also, unlike Dominate, Presence

does ‘not require eye contact. Philosophers hypothesize that Presence’s curse

manifests by replacing true communion with others with artificial intimacy,

driving the Cainite into greater isolation.



Use Leadership for vetests of Presence.

RORM OR CHE BEAST



You can transform your body into that of a wolf or bat. Ie is rumored that

vampires from distant lands can transform into different animals, but most are

limited to these two forms. While you are in animal form, your mind stays yout own

but you have the physical abilities and limitations of the animal.



The Banu Hagim, known to European Cainites as Assamites or Saracens, are the

custodians of this Discipline. Though the warrior caste’s uses of this power is more

familiar, the less familiar sorcerer and vizier castes use it as well in their pursuits.

According to clan lore, Haqim himself developed Quietus after prolonged meditation

and self-contemplation. Ironically, the blood poisoning this Discipline teaches may be

in part to blame for the clan's susceptibility to blood curses. Though the individual

Saracen is no more susceptible, it appears that such things pass through. the clan asa

whole far more readily than with other clans. Beyond this hypothesis, European

scholarship doesnothave much to say about Quietus, for information about it is sorare.



Expend a Blood Trait. Over the next three turns, you transform into a bat of

a wolf. You can reduce the time of the transformation by one turn for each

additional Blood Trait you expend toa minimum of one turn. You can retain your

form until the next dawn or end it when you will. Clothing and small personal

items transform with you. You can use normal Disciplines other than Serpentis,

Youcan create unnatural silence ina certain area. Warriors tend to use this ability

to prevent any sound from emanating from near them. Sorcerers and viziers more often

use it to keep all sound away from a room, whether originating within or without.



The animal forms are physically identical to ordinary animals, but they are

undead. As a wolf, you gain the bonus Traits Alert and Attentive as well as the effects

of Talons of the Beast and running speed greater than that of anyone not using

Celerity. As a bat, you can fly and possess the Merit: Acute Senses (Hearing), but you

are reduced to three Physical Traits (your choice) while in that form.

REGO MOTUS



The ability to cause objects to move without actually touching them

obvious utility to all warlocks. Not only does it allow for one to summon 4 talisman

from across the room in an otherwise desperate situation, but it can be used

propel oneself from the duke’s castle to the chantry without troubling the'd

retainers. None of the powers of Rego Motus allow the thaumaturge to ‘feel thez

objects she manipulates. For example, the sword she summons to her hand co

be searing hot, acid-coated or constructed of wax, and she would not khow un

she grasped it.

You can transform your body inte any of the primary elements other than fire,

froma patch of air or fog toa pool of water toa human-sized boulder or clod of earth.

hatacters who start the game with one or more of them in place, should buy them

dvanced rituals can only be used on Gargoyles of eighth generation or lower.

Rocx=Paper-Scissors



What we mean by Rock-Paper-Scissors is the following: You and

another person face off and, on the count of three, you show one of three

hand gestures. “Rock” isa basic fist. “Paper” is just a flat hand. Stickingout

your middle and index fingers represents “Scissors.” You then compare the

two gestures to determine the winner. Rock crushes Scissors. Scissors curs

Paper. Paper covers Rock. Identical signs indicate a tie. Certain powers

allow some characters to use gestures other than these three.



A fourth gesture, the Bomb; is allowed due to a character usinw

certain supernatural powers. The Bomb is shown by a closed fist with an

upright thumb (the “fuse”). The Bomb beats Rock and Paper, but is

defeated by Scissors (Which cuts the’ fuse). Before players can use this

gesture ina test, however, they must declare that they have the option,

and explain what thé Bomb is, aiid how it is used. Experienced players

may forgo need for the explanation as long as all involved agree.



You may lie about the number of Traits that you currently p , but:on

declaring fewer Trai ve. Bluffing in this way allows yot

NEGATIVE TRAITS



Many characters have Negative Traits that an opponent can-use against th

During the initial bid of any challenge, after each player has bid one Trait but before

test is thrown, a player can call out a Negative Trait that he believes his oppon

possesses. If the player does indeed possess that Negative Trait, he must bid an additio

Trait in order to continue the challenge (although the player who guessed the Negai

Trait does not have to increase his own bid). If the player does not possess the Nega

Trait his opponent called out, his opponent must himself risk an additional Trait Yo

may calloutasmany Negative Traitsas youwish during the initial bid phase ofachalleng

as long as you can pay the price for being wrong. You should also have a valid, in-g

reason to list an opponent’s Negative Traits in the first place. It is ame to rate offa lon

list of possible Negative Traits randomly just to see which guesses stick.



If you figure out more of your opponent’s Negative Traits in a challenge ¢

he has regular Traits to cover, then he loses the challenge automatically. The sam

works in reverse, however, if you do not have additional Traits remaining to mate

incorrect guesses.



Example: Kharkas the Gangrel is attacking Anstruth, a Tremere. He begins



his initial bid (“1 make a Ferocious attack with my claws!”) while Anstruth attempt

dodge (“My Lithe frame is elsewhere than in your grasp.”). Kharkas then suggests the

Anstruth possesses the Negative Trait Clumsy (“All those hours behind a desk have don

litle to hone your reflexes, oh Clumsy one.”) If Anstruth did indeed have Clumsy.on hi

sheet, he would have to bid an additional Trait to continue the challenge: The Tremer

does not possess that Negative Trait, though (“Methinks you misjudge me”); and not

Kharkas — having underestimated his prey —~ is the one who must bid an extra Ta

he wishes to continue to maul his enenvy.



Ie can be risky to bid Negative Traits, but if you’re sure about what you!

doing, you can raise the stakes for your opponent, possibly to the point where h

relents rather than risking additional Traits, Any Traits bid, whether initially

due to Negative Trait calls, are lost if the player loses the challenge.



RETESTS



Certain Traits allow a character to retest a challenge he has lost. -A‘reté

allows a player to ignore the results of the first test (including the loss of Traits). 48

test again for a new result. Multiple retests are possible on a single challenge,

each retest must come from a different source — Abilities, Willpower, Merits

supernatural powers. A character who is trying to strike someone with a sword M

retest his Physical Challenge once using a level of Melee, but he may not gal

another retest using the Melee Ability on the same challenge, even if heh

multiple levels of the Ability. He may, however, use a retest from the Lucky Met



A character who is capable of matching the conditions of the retest. M@

“block” an opponent’s retest. For example, if a player uses Brawl to retest a faile

Physical Challenge to punch his foe, his foe may expend a level of Dodge to bloc

the retest and force the attacker to accept the results of the original test: T

exception to this rule is Willpower.



Example: Baker, a Brujah, is attempting to wrestle Taylor, a Gangrel, 1m?

submission hold. The rebel tries to bear-hug his opponent ( “There is no escape from my Wi



aA ABBEBIR oe



ace, Animal!” ) while the snarling Gangrel steps back, trying to gain distance (“I’m far

Nimble for your fumbling paws to reach me. ”) They perform a test, and Taylor wins.

wever, Baker is an experienced pit-fighter (“My skill gives me victory in this Brawl.”),

he calls for a retest. Taylor states: “You are not the only one skilled in Brawling,” and

locks the retest attempt. Taylor dances out of the reach of the fuming Brujah.



In desperation, Baker dives forward, attempting a tackle (‘My Stalwart arms will

rush the fight out of you,”). Taylor tries to resist witha classic move (“Pardon my Brutal

nee to your groin,”) and they perform ano ther challenge. Baker loses and immediately

alls fora retest (“I'll outlast you in any Brawl.”) Taylor has run out of Brawl Traits,

y he cannot block. They test again and Baker is successful. Taylor squirms in Baker’s

ip to no avail, and groans as his ribs creak painfully.



OVERBIDDING



Overbidding is the system by which powerful elders may prevail in a chal-

enge, even if they lose the initial test. Janos the elder with 13 Mental Traits should

e able to outwit Darian the neonate who has only three. This system is designed

émake that possible.

Oncea test has been made, the loser has the option of calling for an “overbid.”

norder to call an overbid, you must risk a new Trait, as the original one has already

een lost. The other player, as the current winner of the challenge, does not need

o bid a Trait. At this point, the two players must reveal the number of applicable

raits they currently possess in the appropriate category, starting with the player

vho called for the overbid. If that player calls double (or more) the number of

taits his opponent has in that category, he may attempt another test, which is not

ubject to further retests. As ina tie, either player may state a number of Traits less

han-the actual number they have in order to keep their true power secret.

Overbidding can be dangerous unless you are confident in your estimation of your

pponent’s abilities. You can call for only one overbid in a given challenge.

Example: Pietro is attempting to seduce mortal prey. He begins with his looks

| Surely you would prefer to be seen with a Gorgeous man on your arm this evening?”)

but she resists (“One as Elegant as myself needs no man to support her”). Ti hey test,

and the mortal wins, but Pietro is determined to feed. Gambling that his social aptitude

§ superior to the mortal’ s, he bids an additional Trait, relying now on his personality (“But

one as Magnetic as I can only be a bonus to such a strong woman!”) and calls for an

overbid..The mortal, as the defender, does not need to risk an additional Trait. Pietro

anounces all 12 of his current Social Traits (having lost one in the initial test), while the

mortal meekly notes her five. They test again, and this time Pietro is victorious. The mortal

loses her Elegant Trait due to having lost the overall challenge, and Pietro has lost his

Otgeous Trait earlier in the challenge. He has won the challenge, however, as well as

4 botential late supper.

ORDER OF CHALLENGES



Typically, all challenges activate simultaneously in a turn. If you absolutely

must have an order of precedence, the simplest method is for a Narrator to pick a

character at random and then proceed clockwise around the group, arbitrating

each successful challenge.

‘Resolution Determine the results of the challenge



It’s a fact of life that a large group of characters will decide to mix it up sooner

r later. Group challenges can seem intimidating even to experienced Narrators and

Stotytellers. These rules are designed to streamline the resolution process, rather



Since multiple challenges can occur simultaneously during any given fight,

the Narrator occasionally needs some means of determining who acts first and whe

acts last. Each person involved in a given turn should check the current number

of Traits that are appropriate to the action he wishes to attempt. Whoever has.the

highest number of appropriate Traits gets to go first. A character punching

someone would count his Physical Traits, while a character using Dementation

would count her Social Traits.



First of all, find out who is challenging whom. The easiest way to do this is to

unt to three and have everyone point to the person they wish to target that turn.

lfno one is being challenged by more than one person, then the challenges can be



Bonus Traits from weapons and any applicable penalties are not counted.it

this total, just the Traits in the character’s Attribute category. Bonus Traits from

Merits, blood, Disciplines and specializations may be permitted at the discretion.

of the Narrator. Adjustments may need to be made in the case of certain weapons

that allow you to attack before slower weapons. Such cases are specified in hie:

Combat section.



solved normally.



If several characters challenge one target, resolve ir in the following manner.

itst, deal with the groups in the order of largest to smallest, just for ease of play.

Each attacker must bid an appropriate Trait as normal for the challenge. For the

ake of logistics, no more than five characters can attack another character at once.

Next, the lone character must bid enough Traits to counter every opponent

inthe group. If he does nat have enough Traits, he must relent to those opponents

whose bids he cannot meet. He may choose whichopponents he relents to. Resolve

those relented challenges first, because the defender may succumb before the rest



Ifan action does not require any sort of Trait challenge or Trait expenditure,

it comes last in the challenge sequence. If the action requires a simple expenditure

of Willpower or blood, it takes place according to the current Trait level of that

category. Any Discipline effect that has specific Traits attributable to it (e.g-, AM

of Ahyiman) uses those specific Traits for their count in this order.



of the proup can act.

After the bidding and relenting phase, the defender and his attackers engage:

one simultaneous test. The defender compares his sign to each of the attackers" s

and applies the appropriate results. If the defender throws Scissorsand his fourattac

throw Rock, Scissors, Paper and Paper, the defender loses to the first challenger, —

with the second (which is resolved as with any other tie) and wins against the last



The defenders and attackers lose any Traits they have bid ina lost test. If the defen

in the previous example had bid one Trait against every attacker, he would hav, :

one Trait to the first attacker and another if he lost the tie as well.



Once the tests have been made, you resolve them in the standard arde

actions and initiative (ifusing the optional rule). If none of the attackers lose,

defender simply suffers the results of their actions. It is possible fora defender to

Traits to the first attackers and then lose a tie to an attacker later in the Same me

challenge because of those Traits he lost.



Unless the defender hasa special power that allows him to make multiple action

ALONE AGAINST THE WORLD

of people, then he must still undertake a mob challenge. He bids Traits for each

the defenders, up to a maximum of five Traits, no matter the number of defender

Each defender bids a Trait in defense, unless they relent to the challenge. Traits a

lost as normal, but since the attacker has risked no more than five Traits, he cane:

no more than five Traits, no matter how many tests he loses.



CIME



Time in Mind’s Eye Theatre works as it does in real life. I: moves forwat

inexorably, relentlessly.

For the most part, every action plays out in real time, and players are expect

to stay “in character” unless they have a rules question. A player should nevet dro

out of character when interacting with other players. Doing so ruins the: atme

sphere for everyone involved. Players may talk through challenges, bat a charact

is always considered to be active in the game. If a player needs to take a break, A

should inform a Narrator, That player should not interact with any of the othe

players while he is out of character. :

The only other exception to this “in-character rule” is when a Nartator calls fo

a timeout. This call may be necessary to resolve a dispute or change the scene ifth

story calls for it. When “Timeout!” is called, all players within hearing distance see

stop whatever they are doing until the Narrator calls out “Resume!” or “Lay 08:

Timeouts should be kept to a minimum, since they interrupt the flow of the sto



RA ANB BIR



‘(fRONICLES, SCORICS, SESSIONS AND SCENES



- Mind’s Eye Theatre time breaks down into five major allotments: chronicles wore

jong, scenes and turns. A chronicle is a series of smaller stories that are . connected

chow, and which might take monthsor even years tocomplete. Each complete P ne

jn the chronicle is called a story. A session is one actual night of play, a } rou 1

rorytellers may define a session as one night of game time ifthe act ion ends in med i res at

eendof the previous game. (Since many characters regain spent Traits Renee ‘e SIONS,

distinction can be important.) Finally, a scene is the time it takes to resolve the - ie

né location. Once the characters shift locations, the scene isended. Ifa session will be

aking place entirely at one location, a scene can be defined as roughly one hour.



“Tarnsare the discrete blocks of time that make up conflicts and scenes. When

yers start throwing challenges around or attempting complex actions, it is tine

start using turns to measure game time. Turns last approximately three secon s,

at this measure may vary from challenge to challenge at the Storyteller’s

liscretion. In any given turn a character may take one action (although “ome

uperhatural powers may allow extra actions in a turn). Some actions fa ‘ P ace

ver multiple turns, such as picking a complex lock. Other actions, suc Yas

eakitig a short sentence, do not take up a character's action at all. Once ever yone

volved in a turn has taken an action, that turn ends and the next turn begins.

In’some instances, a character might be interrupted before he can take his

ction, or be forced to respond to events developing around him. In such insane

haracter may always defend himself, although doing so uses up his available

action:for the next turn.



OWNTIME



 -Manyaspectsofacharacter’sunlife are critical tohercontinued existences ye they

do‘not make for dramatic roleplaying, or they are too intricate to take time ¢ uring

sessions to perform. Storytellers are encouraged to use “downtime between sessions to

allow characters to maintain their holdings, learn Disciplines and sce to other facets of

their existence. Other actions and interactions may take place during this time, with

Storyteller supervision. As long as players don’t abuse downtime privileges, the time

tween sessions can be a rewarding roleplaying experience in itself.

DAMAGE TYPES



Characters can suffer injury from a broad range of sources. A character!

physical nature determines his vulnerability to injury and the degree to which h

is affected. A Cainite can shrug off injury that would cripple a mortal, yet sustaia

damage from sources that a human wouldn’t consider a risk at all. The Narratot!

the final arbiter of which category of damage a specific event causes:



BASHING DAMAGE



Bashing damage is unlikely to kill, and even mortals heal it swiftly. Bruises, sprains and 28

minor injuries such as those from falls, punches or clubs are included. Cainites are. largely

unaffected by such minor injuries due to the lack of blood in their body tissues, so theysuffe

only half (round down, minimum of one level) the indicated damage from such Causes:



While bashing damage is rarely fatal, it does soften the victim up for worse ©

come. If a Cainite is reduced to Incapacitated by bashing damage, subsequent

aggravated damage will cause Final Death. Additional bashing or lethal damag

will simply place them in torpor. =



or Incapacitated mortals, any additional bashing damage converts current

health levels from bashing into lethal damage as bones break and organs crush.

ey take any level of actual lethal damage, they become Mortally Wounded, as

hey will die if subsequent bashing damage pushes them past Incapacitated again.

== Example: Joshua has been beaten senseless by thugs, and he lies Incapacitated in the

| Francis, his rival for the hand of alady, takes the opportunity to plant a boot in Joshua’s

This dct causes one level of bashing damage normally, but it converts Joshua’s first lost

Ithy level into a lethal loss. Joshua must now nurse 4 broken rib, rather than just tending



his bruises. If Francis had instead stabbed his vival with a dagger, Joshua would be dying...



ETHAL DAMAGE



Asthe name suggests, lethal damage is far more serious, and it has the potential

illormaim, especially if the victim is mortal. Most bladed weapons inflict lethal

ae, as might some blunt weapons (noted in their individual descriptions).

Unlike bashing damage, lethal damage has a much more immediate effect on

ttals. Any mortal reduced below Incapacitated by lethal damage is dying. A

nite in a similar position is simply driven into torpor, but be does not reach

nal Death as a result. Such injuries still make the vampire vulnerable to Final

eath through subsequent aggravated damage, though.



AGGRAVACED DAMAGE



Although Cainites are far more resilient in general than mortals, some forms

njury-are dire even to them. Largely elemental or supernatural in origin (e.g.,

fire, sunlight, the teeth and claws of other vampires, or any other source the

Jatrator deems sufficient due to circumstances}, these sources of injury are hard

6 resist and equally hard to heal.



Mortals suffer lethal damage from those things that would cause a Cainite to take

peravated damage (except sunlight, of course). There are some specific instances in

ich a mortal may receive aggravated damage, however, and they typically require

etnatural means to heal them. These are explained on.a case-by-case basis.



Sunlight



_ Exposure to sunlight is extremely painful for vampires. Indirect sunlight, such

s through thick curtains or heavy cloud cover causes one automatic aggravated

und per turn of exposure, while direct sunlight causes three levels per curn and

‘obably causes the vampire to burst into flame. Even gazing into a sunlit area may

use temporary blindness as the reflected rays burn the vampire’s eyes. Heavy

othing provides some protection, reducing damage or the rate at which it is

fered, at the Storyteller’s discretion. Vampires confronted by sunlight must also

ake a Courage Test for Rétschreck.

Cainites fear and loathe fire, and its slightest touch causes them great agony.

Ost vampires are uncomfortable around open flame, since it can destroy them

ethanently, Sufficiently large sources of flame inevitably provoke Courage Tests

Cainites to avoid Rétschreck.

direst types of damage are considered to sit at the top end of a character's healt

HEALING

CAINICE HEALING



Vampires heal through the simple expenditure of blood. Such an action

reflexive and takes no actions to accomplish, although the Cainite is still restrict?

to the limits of his blood expenditure as per his generation. Healing.a level

bashing or lethal damage takes the expenditure of one Blood Trait. "



Example: If Marie expends four Blood Traits over the next few turns to heal, she

he Bruised, but she is still suffering a lethal wound and an aggravated wound (taking

lace of her ewo Healthy levels). Later that night, after feeding, she then heals the

naining lethal wound with one more Blood Trait.



In order to heal one level of aggravated damage, the Cainite must spend three

god Traits. The damage heals over the following day as the vampire sleeps. This

sod can be expended over a period of several days of rest — simply keep a note

he character sheet of how much blood has been expended for the health level

ing healed. If the vampire wishes to attempt to heal more than one level of

avated damage in one day, she must expend a Willpower Trait for each

(ditional aggravated health level h saled in the same rest period (in addition to

e three Blood Traits per aggravated health level).

iedical expertise of the Dark Medieval is also quite primitive compared to modern

ealth level must be healed individually, so a mortal who bas reached Incapaci-

ed from bashing damage must spend one week recovering to the Wounded level,



da further three days recovering to Bruised.

- Bashing damage is largely superficial, and it will heal without treatment. The

ainfactor is time, although medical attention may accelerate the process.

Lethal damage is far more serious, and it can result in complications such as

fection. Scars are commonplace. Characters injured with lethal damage to the

uised level who do not receive medical attention automatically lose an addi-

onal health level each day to reflect infection and blood loss. After initial medical

tention, further treatment is not required, so long as the character is above

ounded. Incapacitated characters require constant medical attention and are

robably delirious or unconscious.

ditional lethal wound, possibly dying if this rakes her below Incapacitated.

CORPOR



The Cainite state of torpar isakin toacoma. A torpid vampire is index

sleep — apparently dead to non-Cainites — and she is oblivious to events

outside world. Torpid vampires ignore the nightly need for blood: th

effectively in hibernation for the time they remain in that state:



There are three primary methods for entering torpor — voluntatily,

injury and due to deterioration. Entering torpor voluntarily is simple: The

simply wills ic so, which takes but a few seconds, and no challenge’is iny:

Entering torpor through injury is self-explanatory. Cainites without ace

until they collapse into torpor. This process of deterioration is described in

detail later in this section.



li Se

entered their torpor voluntarily may attempt to awaken after-only ha

indicated time.

Blood Trait) until she succeeds or runs out of blood. If she has no blood, she

not rise until some is given to her.

she is fed at least one Blood Trait. Unless fed, she remains in this state indefini

but she may attempt to rise as soon as she consumes new vitae, irrespective O

Road Traits. Such “early revivification” only works for Cainites who enter to

because of blood loss. Those who enter voluntatily or because of injury must $

intervention, :

DRUGS AND POISONS



Mortals use a variety of substances and herbs to heal, harm Gr alter perceptio:



Most cannot be used directly by Cainites, though they may be imbibed: indirec

through the blood of unwitting or victims or. willing vessels. Rather than detailing!

effect of every drug and poison, the following are the most common and typical effee

Alcohol — A vampire drinking blood that contains alcohol suffers some



the effects of being drunk. For every two drinks consumed by the victim, t

Cainite gains the Negative Physical Trait Chemsy and the Negative Mental Tre

Oblivious. This effect dissipates at the rate of one Negative Trait pet hourorscen

Bloodroot (Sanguinaria) — The rare and deadly bloodroot is one.of the k

poisons that is directly harmful to Cainites. Consuming it (forexample, mixed wi

blood) causes three health levels of aggravated damage, while using it as a. cont

poison (such as on a blade) inflicts two health levels of aggravated damag

addition to any injury caused by the weapon. The poison attacks vampiric ¥

turning if into an ashlike black dust.

Food Poisoning (Salmonella} — Blood tainted with salmonella causes naus



and a level of bashing damage per Blood Trait consumed to the feeding vamp!

Additionally, she has difficulty drinking blood until purged of the bad plood(

under “Diseases”), but she may force herself to drink (see'the feeding rules und

“Plague”). The effects of food poisoning wear off after about a day.

Hashish — In common use in the Middle East, hashish has a calming effect;

italso affects the imbiber’s attentiveness. A vampire drinking hashish-tainted blood

gains the Negative Mental Trait Oblivious. Hashish also reduces the difficulty oe

resisting frenzy by one Trait. These effects last for approximately one hour:

Hallucinogens -— Hallucinogenic drugs such as cowbane, henban¢e 2

deadly nightshade (belladonna) are used as both painkillers and poisons in

Dark Medieval. A vampire drinking blood that contains stnall quantities of su

herbs is considered one to three Traits down (depending on the amount consum

by the victim and vampire) in any challenges because of impaired concentral



he character also suffers effects equivalent to Haunt the Soul. Other effects occur

the Storyteller’s discretion, but they may include gaininga temporary Basic level



‘Auspex or losing a Trait of Courage. The effects of hallucinogens last for a number

f hours, possibly until the end of the game session, but they may clear if there is

«nificant time lapse between two scenes involving the character.



Painkillers -—— As with hallucinogens, herbs such as hemlock, mandrake and

nkshood are used as both painkillersand poisons. In small doses, they reduce the

isabling effects of injury, dropping the wound penalty for lost health levels.

jruised characters have no penalties, Wounded characters suffer Bruised penal-

ies, Incapacitated characters suffer Wounded penalties. Allother health levels are



naffected. The effects last as for hallucinogens.



Poison — Larger doses of hallucinogens or painkillers, or extracts such as

eni¢, strychnine or cyanide, can prove fatal to mortals and harmful to Cainites.

While a mortal might suffer an agonizing death, a Cainite is down one to three Traits

nall challenges and takes between one and three health levels of lethal damage,

Jepending on the strength of the poison and the amount of tainted blood he’s drunk.

isons cannot kill Cainites or drive them into torpor, but they can temporarily



A character’s mental state is as important as her physical health, and it is much

less controllable in many cases. A vampire can use blood points to heal a physical

ound, but mental injuries and states are more difficult to deal with.



RENZY AND ROCSCHRECK



ln imany waysan ultimate illustration of the “fight-or-flight” reflex, the Beast lurks

neath the surface of all vampires and manifests as a vicious form of madness when

ought forth. Most Cainites resist the Beast desperately, straining to keep it under

ntrol, When they fail, the resulting orgy of instinctual violence can level friends and

es alike — the Beast does not discriminate. The vampire feels no pain and acts on

- — thstinct, using his bare hands and fangs to rip apart anything around him. Usually the

= fusttargetisthe creature that triggered the frenzy, or anythingand anyone betweenhim

nd his target, Otherwise, the closest object or creature to hand will suffer.

The triggers of the Beast are often highly personalized, but triggers common

all vampires are blood hunger, extreme passion, frustration, defeat, humiliation

t the hands of a rival or threats to a vampire’s friends or loved ones. Players must

consistent with what causes a frenzy in their characters; a player cannot ignore

omething that would normally trigger a frenzy simply because it isn’t convenient

ot him to frenzy at this time. The Beast doesn’t care. Discretion is advised,

oWever; a character in constant frenzy is no fun to be around and will likely be “put

own” by other vampires.

Succumbing to the Beast is considered shameful and debased among many

Ainites, and it might result in the character losing status. Vampires will be held

Fesponsible for their frenzied actions by other vampires. The social repercussions

May be worse than the situation that brought forth the Beast in the first place.

When in frenzy, a Cainite has the following .

advantages and disadvantages:

* He ignores all wound penalties until he reaches torpor or Final Death. -

* He cannot initiate Social Challenges unless that challenge is related _

to intimidation. ;

© He does not need to risk any Social Traits if a Social Challenge is

called against him.

® He is immune to further-checks for frenzy or Rotschreck.

To avoid Rétschreck, the vampire must make a Static Courage Challenge

(Courage versus the Narraton’s difficulty, no Traits risked). Systemically, Ratschreck

is identical to frenzy for the purposes of determining duration, except that Courage

is used rather than Self-Control. You cannot use the rules for riding the Beast in the 2

case of Rétschreck, however. All vampires must fight the Beast or flee in frenzy.



A vampire entering Rétschreck. flees the object. of her fear as directly:and

rapidly as she can, blindly attacking any obstacles or people that get in her way, lf

flight proves impossible, she will attempt to destroy the object of her fear then flee

Ifsuch options are not available, she curls up in abject terror for the duration of the

Rétschreck. Note that this fear does not override her self-preservation instincts

she will not leap from a tower’s height to avoid a candle —- but any path that.is not

obviously suicidal becomes an option.



i



Without hope, many Cainites would give themselves to the Beast and revel

in their monstrous nature. Various paths of control are available to vampires to

quell their Beast, and a number of philosophies have been suggested as to how to

finally bind the Beast in a position of total submission. Cainite mychology. espouses

the state of Golconda, a legendary state of transcendence that reflects mastery over

the Beast. Rumors exist of those who have achieved such a glorious goal, but they,

usually take the form of “a friend of a friend,” with no direct witnesses: :



Many vampires on the Road of Heaven have sought Golconda, following a

loose process known as the Bitter Journey, but few, if any, have attained it; With

the growth of the presence of devout Christian, Muslim and Jewish. vampires, -

Golconda is becoming condemned as a pagan practice, at odds with the concept

of God’s redemption. Indeed, more fanatical Cainites have been known to‘hunt

down and slay heretics rumored to be undertaking the Bitter Journey.



Whether Golconda exists and is achievable is up to individual Storytellers, There

are no fixed systems for Golconda due to its inherently ephemeral nature. Each Cainite



must discover her own path to enlightenment — and Storytellers are encouraged to be

extremely demanding when it comes to Golconda quests. This journey can easily take

up years of play and constant progress through multiple stories. The only solid rule is

that the Cainite must maintain a Road rating and Conscience rating of at least fout

Traits to remain on the path to Golconda. Slipping below that level will generally cause

mentors on the path to desert the Cainite until he atones for his degeneration:



The following philosophies offer guidelines for such a quest to be part of a.

chronicle. One or more of these effects may be granted to a character who has

clearly indicated through excellence in roleplay over the course of his quest that

he has achieved control in that area. :



Acceptance: Those who have attained Golconda accept themselves for what

they are. They do not rail on about their “damned” status, nor.do. they sulfet

jealousy of mortal life. They are simply part of existence.



Calm: Those who attain Golconda are reputed to have mastered their Beast

ad never fear succumbing to frenzy or Roétschreck, including immunity to

sciplines that cause such effects. ;

Hunger: Although they are still tied to the requirements of blood, a Cainite

tho has attained Golconda needs to feed much less often (perhaps only required

a spend one blood point per week, rather than per day).



Strength: A Cainite who has attained Golconda is not fully bound by the

hackles of generation, so she may learn Disciplines in excess of her usual limits.

Albother generational limits remains unaffected.



Mortality: Perhaps the most seductive of the legends associated with Geleonda

sthat, through enlightenment, a vampire may throw off Caine’s curse and return

‘o mortality. How such a transformation might be effected is spoken of only in

vhispers, but self-sacrifice, true love and devotion are recurring themes. Even

those who believe in Golconda usually regard these stories of transformation as

anciful, but as always, the truth of the matter is in the hands of the Storyteller.



CHE BLOOD OATH



One of the strangest properties of Cainite vitae is its ability to forge a link

between the vampire and the drinker. This power is used to create mortal servants,

butit can also be used to bind other vampires to the Cainite’s will. The strength

of this bond depends on the number of times the victim has drank the blood of the

same-Cainite, but after three such sips, the drinker is almost irrevocably bound.

The person (living or unliving) who comes under this bond, called the blood oath,

is known as the thrall, while the Cainite holding power over them is the remnant.



A fully bound thrall is utterly devoted to her regnant and cannot take action

against her. In many cases, this feeling is like a mortal addiction or obsession. The

thrall: may not necessarily love his regnant (though many do}, and he may even

actively despise her, but he follows her orders nonetheless, even if he is dominated

or otherwise manipulated by outside agencies. Many Cainites have described the

oath as a compelling force, but it is not necessarily a compulsion to do exactly as

the regnant says. Rather the thrall is honor-bound to demonstrate loyalty, to obey

ofders and rhe express wishes of the regnant. This distinction between compelled

obedience and loyalty is a fine line, but it allows the thrall to demonstrate some

flexibility. Invariably, however, the thrall follows his master’s wishes, the way of

oath-bound loyalty in the Dark Medieval for mortals and Cainites alike. Going

against the master’s wishes is simply unconscionable.



The power of the oath is not dependent on the regnant’s generation. The

lood of a 12th-generation neonate can bind an elder as readily as the elder binds

others to her will. This is the only innate Cainite power that does not appear to

degrade with generation. A Cainite may be fully oathbound to only one regnant,

but she may have several thralls and lesser bonds (those involving one or two

ltinks) herself.

/ERANGEMENTS



Mental trauma, boredom due to centuries of tedium or continual loss —- all

‘ese factors and many more can lead to the twisting of a Cainite’s perception of

lity; Madness isa very real part of the Dark Medieval, and those who suffer from

are variously seen as cursed or blessed. A Storyteller may decide that a



rangement is in order after any experience that generates especially intense and

pleasant emotions, or which severely violates the character's beliefs or ethics.



While much of this section is written about Cainites, mortals can likewise

fer derangements, though the Storyteller may need to alter aspects of the rules

vided. For example, mortals cannot enter frenzy, but they can attack wildly with

impleve disregard for their actions and the well-being of those around them.

All derangements carry “triggers” — circumstances that cause the effects of

e derangement to surface. These triggers should be assigned appropriate to the

sxperience that caused the derangement, or they might be dependant on the

iture of the derangement itself. Once triggered, the derangement becomes active

ethe duration of the scene, and the player must modify her character's Traits,

titudes and behaviors in accordance with the derangement’s description.

Detangements may be resisted by the expenditure of a Willpower Trait. Such a

spenision lasts foronly the duration of thescene, however, and ifthe trigger isstill present

the end of that time, the character must expend another Willpower Trait of suffer the

ects.of the derangement, Narrators may rule that additional Willpower Traits or

illpower Challenges (treat asa normal challenge, risking Willpower Traits rather than

ttributes) may be required to deal with particularly intense mental stresses.

The quest to cure derangements is fuel for long, intense stories, and the

solution of such stories rests solely in the hands of the Storyteller. Modern

ychotherapeutic methods are hardly accessible in the Dark Medieval, and

merous bizarre and tortuous methods were conceived to rid the insane of their

edevilment. Indeed, many insane people were considered to be possessed by the

Petnatural, and overtly dangerous lunatics sometimes drew unwanted attention

omthe Church. Malkavians may never cure the original derangement(s) brought

n bythe clan disadvantage, but they may work at shedding others that have

therwise sprung from their experiences.



Here isa brief list of derangements and their effects on characters. Storytellers might

h toallow other derangements into play, but they are advised to develop rules such as

hese to avoid confusion over their in-game effects in the future. Often frenzy can he the

Tesult of actual reality jarring the deranged character, and a Self-Controlf Instinct Test is

fequired, with a difficulty decided by the Narrator based on the circumstances.

Note: There is nothing funny or arbitrary about the way a “crazy” person acts. To

im, his behavior is perfectly normal, and he is simply reacting to the stimuli that he

teives tobe real. Players should never forget the Mind’s Eye Theatre rules of safety

when toleplaying derangements. Playingderangements involvesadvanced roleplaying

ill'and is better suited to experienced players. Additionally, derangements are

Amnesia ve



In highly traumatic situations, the character sometimes forgets who:

what he is. This typically occurs when he comes face-to-face with his ve

condition. The character might simply forget the memory of a singlé BF a

he might forget everything about his identity, including his true natut 4

even forget Abilities or Disciplines and be surprised to discover that h

things he thought were beyond his capabilities. When events and situate

might remind him of his lost memories present themselves, those merge

return, sometimes doing so violently and sending the character-into a frénzy



Bulimia :



. Bulimic characters salve their guilt and insecurity by over-indulgin

activities that comfort them — in this instance, consuming food (or blood

vampires). Characters with this affliction will gorge themselves as much as pass

when under stress, then purge their system through drastic means (burnin

Traits, Disciplines or regurgitating blood as described in “Starve a Cold?)

consume more. Characters with this derangement must make a Static Conscie

Conviction Challenge when feeding. Fatlure means that the vampire feeds unti

has reached bis maximum Blood Trait capacity, whether or not he needs the bl

If forcibly kept from feeding, he must resist frenzy.



Crimson Rage



A character with this derangement is prone to experiencing fits ofanger wv

little provocation. While the two bear a certain resemblance, this state is qu

different from frenzy, Frenzy is the instincts of the vampiric Beast, while Crims

Rage is the vampire’s own feelings of helplessness and inadequacy. He is £

protected from being pushed over the edge into frenzy while in the grip oft Zi

derangement, however. Whenever this derangement is active, the characte g

the Negative Mental Traits: Violent x 2 and Impatient.



Fantasy/Delusion

. Some characters cannot accept the real world, so they transpose themsel

into an illusory world instead. As this is something of a “catch-all” derangeme

the scope and degree of this fantasy varies considerably, and details should be sor

out with the Storyteller. While the character interacts with people and institution’

of the Dark Medieval in an almost normal manner, her perception of event

skewed by her fantasy, Something happening to shatter the illusions the characte

has crafted about herself can cast her into frenzy.



Fugue



Characters suffering this affliction react to stress by adopting a specific set al

behaviors. In the process, they suffer “blackouts” or periods of memory loss. Whenevel

the character is confronted by extreme stress, the player must win a Static Willpoy

Challenge against a difficulty determined by che Narrator depending of rhe degree «

stress, Failure means that the character blacks out and the player muist roleplay th



eters trancelike state. Otherwise, control of the character passes to a Narrator for

ene, who dictates the actions the character takes in order to remove the stress. At

adofthe fugue, the character “regains consciousness” with no memory ofhisactions.

Hysteria

Hysterical characters are unable to control their emotions, and they suffer

severe mood swings and fits of intense violence. A hysterical Cainite will

y more easily than other vampires (increase the difficulty of his Self-Contol/

dinct Test by one Trait), particularly when faced with great stress. In addition,

time the vampire fails in a particularly stressful or prominent situation.

arrator’s call) the character will automatically enter frenzy, with no check.

Jmmortal Terror



This madness stems from the vampire’s inability to deal with the true scope

his immortality. Terrified by the real implications of living forever, the vampire

pes by developing a strong unconscious “death wish.” Whenever he is con-

onted: by direct evidence of his immortality — such as attending a funeral or

tching a mortal ally die — the character must make a Static Willpower

hallenge (against four Traits) to avoid immediately taking actions that might

sult in his destruction, Such actions can be as indirect as breaking the Silence of

¢ Blood by confessing to a priest, as long as the act carries potentially deadly

mnsequences. Note that the vampire is not consciously aware that he seeks his

adestruction, and he resists attempts to persuade him otherwise.

- Lumacy

This madness comes and goes, linked to the cycle of the moon. When the

joon is full, the character is manic and delirious, while at the time of the new

oon; he may be reserved and melancholic. At intervening times, he may appear

otmal and unaffected. While in the grip of this derangement, his ability to resist

enay and Rétschreck varies accordingly, increasing or decreasing by a Trait to

eflect his mood depending on his link to the lunar cycle.

Manic-Depression

A:Cainite with this derangement experiences wild mood swings. She fre-

ently slips into deep depression, losing interest in her normal activities and

becoming withdrawn. Alternately, she is gripped by bursts of fervent energy. When

- suffeting from depression, the vampire’s Willpower Traits are greatly reduced (half,

ound up, the normal value — when the phase ends, Willpower Traits return to

heit previous level, minus any spent during that period). These depressive periods

= often follow failure of a particular action, though they may also result from hunger

{ablood pool of one-quarter or less) or psychological factors. Hyperactivity willsee

the vampire working for hours or even into the day on her projects, resisting the

=~ teed tosleep as she burns up blood and Willpower on her schemes. She is also one

Trait down to resist frenzy during this manic time. Should someone attempt to stir

adepressive or thwart a manic vampire, the vampire may frenzy.

Megalomania

Characters with this derangement believe that they are destined to lead, and

they seek to accumulate power, irrespective of their skill and the attitude of others.

They believe that those who dismiss their claims are jealous, seeking to hold onto

Power and deny them their dues. Megalomaniacs believe that these opponents

ChE THORN

Many young vampires believe diablerie to be the perfect crime. The body i

destroyed in the process, making it difficult to secure enough evidence to support

an accusation of murder. Diablerists quickly learn, however, that there are ways 0

never becomes a casual crime.



For most Europeans, this faith is in Jesus Christ, but other faiths are equally

powerful. Jews, Muslims, pagans and even heretics can have as much faith. (or

more) than Christians. The truth of the belief is not as important as the strength

ofthe faithful’s conviction.

most mortals who have it aren’t very conscious of it because they focus on the goe

be considered Traits up for the character. He may also add his Faith rating to his

Conscience rating when making a Conscience Challenge.

* The faithful may cure injury and sickness simply by their touch. The blessing

grants a number of health levels for healing purposes only. For example, a patient

who has suffered lethal wounds to his first Wounded level and received the healing

touch of a priest with True Faith x 3, the patient is granted health levels until he

is considered Bruised for the purposes of healing time and making his Static

Physical Challenge to recover. (In this case, the patient need only rest for a day,

as if he were Bruised, and his difficulty is three Traits.) If the granted levels cause

‘sleeping. He may not sense evil presences while he is distracted {in a crowded

market or a feasting hall during a revel) or while occupied (in debate or combat).

The character does not know exactly what is near him, beyond something unholy.

ROLY ITEMS



The Eaithful can bless items by undergoing religious ceremonics involving

those items. These scenes should be roleplayed out, if a player’s character is

involved. One item can be blessed over half an hour. Only one blessing per session

cat occur from a given character, and any given item can hold only one blessing

atatime. Blessed items have an additional Bonus Trait (Burning, Searing, Blinding,

Branding, Purging, Cleansing or Purifying) which may be bie ina Physical Chailenge

involving the item and in opposition to a supernatural creature. If the challenge

islost, this Trait is gone, and the item loses its blessing. Ifthe challenge is successful,

the item touches the creature, causing one level of aggravated damage (rather than

its normal damage). Bidding a normal Trait means that the item is being used as

normal, and it causes normal damage (if any).

Holy water will likewise cause aggravated damage -~ one level for a brief

splash, or one level per turn of invmersion, although it does not gain any Bonus

Traits. Supernatural creatures handling such objects for extended periods of time

may cause them to lose their blessing.



This power is not completely limited to characters with True Faith. A devout,

honest priest hasa lesser version of this ability which allows him to bless holy water

or the wine and wafers of communion.



RELICS



Special holy items, relics of antiquity, hold further special powers, such as healing

or blessing. These items are extremely rare, imbued with the faith of the masses over

the centuries, and the Storyteller must approve their entry into the game, as well as designate

their special abilities. They are usually kept within special protective cases called

teliquaries. Many medieval churches have at least one relic (sometimes of dubious

otigin), Their power level varies according to the Faith surrounding chem. The finger

bone of a little-known saint will hold less power than a splinter of the True Cross, for

example, Some charlatans peddle fake relics, such as animal bones for saints’ bones,

tags for the mantle of the Virgin or splinters claimed to be fragments of the manger.

Strangely enough, however, these false relics may develop their own Faith rating and

some measure of holy power over time and with enough reverence of the faichful.



Not every relic is necessarily an ancient artifact, Holy water, the sacramental

wine and bread and the badges of pilgrims can have Faith ratings and act as relics.

Not every relic need be Christian -—- pagans, Jews and Muslims all have sacred

objects that are precious to them and their faithful. The exact effects of their relics

are up to the Storyteller.



The touch of a relic inflicts aggravated darnage on supernatural creatures and

causes them to flee if they fail a Courage Test against the level of damage they take.

This level is determined by the Storyteller, although a maximum of four levels is

Tecommended. Other powers that the faithful may call upon from the relic should
